Hydrogen bonds, which involve the attraction between a hydrogen atom covalently bonded to an electronegative atom (such as O, N, or F) and another electronegative atom, provide directionality and specificity in molecular recognition. They help align host and guest molecules, facilitating selective binding and stabilizing the complex. Anion-π interactions, a type of non-covalent interaction where an anion interacts with the electron-deficient π-system of an aromatic ring, further contribute to the stabilization and selectivity of host-guest assemblies, especially when the guest is an anionic species. These interactions can enhance binding affinity and influence the geometry of the complex. Together, hydrogen bonds and anion-π interactions enable the reversible, yet robust, association of host and guest molecules, underpinning the dynamic and functional nature of supramolecular systems. They help align host and guest molecules, facilitating selective binding and stabilizing the complex. Anion-π interactions, a type of non-covalent interaction where an anion interacts with the electron-deficient π-system of an aromatic ring, further contribute to the stabilization and selectivity of host-guest assemblies, especially when the guest is an anionic species.
